class="main-article-content"><div class="ecmRichText" style="margin-bottom:0px"><section><h1><span>All Spring 2024 Network Updates</span></h1><h2 id="spring-2024-release-guide" class="test_h2 markdown-h2"><span>SPRING 2024 RELEASE GUIDE</span><a class="icon icon--link hash-link" href="#spring-2024-release-guide" aria-label="SPRING 2024 RELEASE GUIDE"><img src="https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/_assets/anchor-PKYVW2VT.svg" alt="AnchorIcon"/></a></h2><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  The card networks (Visa, Mastercard, Amex, Discover, etc.) introduce and make changes to their
  operating rules and mandates throughout the year. Many of these changes come twice per yearâ€”in
  spring and fall.
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  These network updates typically include fee introductions or fee changes, new mandates, new
  features, or updates to existing features. The changes can be broad in nature and may include
  updates such as mandates to comply with new regulations; implementing new fees; or requiring
  merchants to use schemes like 3DS 2.0 to help reduce fraud.
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><u><span>While many of the updates require no action for merchants, some do require integration changes
    or force adoption of services. Additionally, some of the updates carry new or changed fees.</span></u></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>PayPal Braintree teams have worked together to identify the key updates for Spring 2024, and we
    have provided information about these updates below.</span></strong><span>
  We have called out the type of update (fee change, mandate, new feature/update), which network the
  update comes from, and the relevant market(s).
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>new</span></p><h2 id="key-spring-2024-network-releases" class="test_h2 markdown-h2"><span>KEY SPRING 2024 NETWORK RELEASES</span><a class="icon icon--link hash-link" href="#key-spring-2024-network-releases" aria-label="KEY SPRING 2024 NETWORK RELEASES"><img src="https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/_assets/anchor-PKYVW2VT.svg" alt="AnchorIcon"/></a></h2><p class="markdown-p"><span>(click below to jump to specific update)</span></p><style data-emotion="css href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/mc-s24#what-is-the-revised-excessive-authorization-attempts--ca--mandate"><span>Revised Excessive Authorization Attempts</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="120"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Fee Change</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="114"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Canada</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="395"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/mc-s24#what-is-the-cvv2-compliance-requirements-mandate"><span>CVV2 Compliance Requirements</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="120"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Feature Change</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="114"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>APAC</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="395"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/mc-s24#what-is-the-extending-network-access-and-brand-usage-fee-change"><span>Extending Network Access and Brand Usage Fee</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="120"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Fee Change</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="114"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>US</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="395"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/mc-s24#what-is-the-revising-acquirer-brand-volume-fee-change"><span>Revising Acquirer Brand Volume Fee</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="120"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Fee Change</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="114"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>US</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h2 id="all-mastercard-network-updates" class="test_h2 markdown-h2"><span>All Mastercard Network Updates</span><a class="icon icon--link hash-link" href="#all-mastercard-network-updates" aria-label="All Mastercard Network Updates"><img src="https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/_assets/anchor-PKYVW2VT.svg" alt="AnchorIcon"/></a></h2><h1><span>What is the Expansion of the Digital Enablement Fee in the US mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>Master</span></span><span><span>card</span></span></strong><span> |
  US
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 15 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  From 15 April 2024, Mastercard will revise the pricing for the Digital Enablement Fee (DEF) and
  charge a fixed rate of $0.40 USD for card-not-present (CNP) transactions greater than or equal to
  $1000 USD. The Digital Enablement Fee of 0.02% (2 basis points) with a minimum of $0.20 USD
  remains for transactions less than $1000 USD.
</span></p><h1><span>What is the Revised Excessive Authorization Attempts (CA) mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>Master</span></span><span><span>card</span></span></strong><span> |
  CA
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 1 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  From 1 April 2024, Mastercard will revise the threshold for the Excessive Authorization Attempts
  Transaction Processing Excellence (TPE) program in Canada, introducing a threshold of 35 declined
  attempts on the same account number, at the same card acceptor, and for the same amount within a
  30-day period.
</span></p><div role="alert" class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__1QhIq ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert--note__gRM6J"><div class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__header__T2Wkg"><style data-emotion="css 4757ty-svg-size_xs">.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs{speak:none;display:inline-block;aspect-ratio:1;width:1.125rem;height:1.125rem;}.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs img,.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs svg{width:100%;height:100%;display:block;}</style><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__icon__puACD css-4757ty-svg-size_xs" data-ppui-info="icons_8.21.2" role="img" aria-label="note" data-ppui="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-ppui="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M21 12a9 9 0 1 1-18 0 9 9 0 0 1 18 0zm-9.662 5h1.32c.18 0 .276-.096.276-.276v-5.925c0-.18-.096-.276-.276-.276h-1.32c-.18 0-.276.096-.276.276v5.925c0 .18.096.276.276.276zM12 9a1 1 0 1 0 0-2 1 1 0 0 0 0 2z" clip-rule="evenodd" data-ppui="true"></path></svg></span><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__title__FOcbD">Note</span><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__content__2-Ddi"><p class="markdown-p"><span>The first billing for the new Canada TPE threshold will occur on 5 May 2024.</span></p></span></div></div><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  To avoid the excessive authorization attempts TPE fees, Mastercard is recommending that acquirers
  immediately stop sending authorizations on the same card and same card acceptor ID, within a
  24-hour period after receiving 10 consecutive decline responses, as well as to stop sending
  authorizations on the same card, same card acceptor, for the same amount, within a 30-day period
  after receiving 35 decline responses.
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  The applicable fee will be 0.50 USD per identified declined transaction. To avoid TPE fees,
  merchants should review their statements to identify TPE charges then adjust behavior to avoid
  these fees.
</span></p><h1><span>What is the CVV2 Compliance Requirements mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEATURE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span><span>Master</span></span><span><span>card</span></span></strong><span> | APAC
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 8 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Mastercard will be eliminating the Card Verification Value 2 (CVV2) verification for both
  card-on-file (COF) and guest checkout experiences in the Asia Pacific region. This change will
  apply to all Mastercard Digital Enablement Service (MDES) tokenized transactions. By leveraging
  tokenization and approved authentication methods available through the EMV 3-D Secure and Token
  Authentication Framework (TAF), consumers can complete transactions securely without the need for
  CVV2 verification.
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  No merchant action is immediately required, but they should plan for when issuers are ready to
  incorporate the change.
</span></p><h1><span>What is the Extending Network Access and Brand Usage Fee change?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>Master</span></span><span><span>card</span></span></strong><span> |
  US
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 15 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  From 15 April 2024, Mastercard is extending the Network Access and Brand Usage fee (NABU) for
  Non-domestic Authorizations, Collection-only, and Refund/Credit transactions in the United States,
  increasing the fees for US merchants who process transactions from non-US issued cards to $0.0295
  per transaction. NABU feesâ€”sometimes also referred to as card association fees or card brand
  feesâ€”are the fees associated with processing a transaction with a card network like Mastercard.
</span></p><style data-emotion="css class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h1><span>What is the Revising Acquirer Brand Volume Fee change?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>Master</span></span><span><span>card</span></span></strong><span> |
  US
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 15 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  From 15 April 2024, Mastercard will introduce two enhanced tools (Merchant Risk Dashboard; Small
  Business Credit Analytics) designed to streamline acquirersâ€™ efforts to identify and mitigate
  potential risks during both the initial onboarding process and daily operations. In addition,
  Mastercard will raise the Acquirer Brand Volume fee by 0.01% from 0.13% to 0.14%. This updated fee
  will apply to all Mastercard transactions.
</span></p><h2 id="all-visa-network-updates" class="test_h2 markdown-h2"><span>All Visa Network Updates</span><a class="icon icon--link hash-link" href="#all-visa-network-updates" aria-label="All Visa Network Updates"><img src="https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/_assets/anchor-PKYVW2VT.svg" alt="AnchorIcon"/></a></h2><h1><span>What are the Visa Processing Integrity Fees?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |</span><strong><span>CEMEA, CA, AP, EU, Latin America and the Caribbean</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date:</span></strong><span> 1 April 2024 (APAC excluding Japan); 25 April 2024 (CEMEA, EU,
  LAC excluding Brazil and Chile); 25 May 2024 (Canada)
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Visa will begin compliance monitoring for the Processing Integrity Program with the introduction
  of 2 new fees:
</span></p><ul class="list list--disc"><li><strong><span>Misuse of Authorization System</span></strong><span>: assessed to approved or partially approved auth
    transactions that cannot be matched to a clearing transactions or authorization reversal.
  </span></li><li><strong><span>Unmatched Clearing</span></strong><span>: assessed on clearing transactions that cannot be matched to
    previously approved or partially approved auth transactions.
  </span></li></ul><style data-emotion="css 19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100">.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{color:#202020;font-family:PayPalOpen-Regular,"Helvetica class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" width="720"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>*EU rate rises to $0.05 per transaction in July 2024.</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h1><span>What are the Modifications to Certain US Interchange Rates and Programs?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>US</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date:</span></strong><span> 13 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Interchange adjustments based on Visa products used by the merchants' consumers. Merchants will
  see continued interchange savings when transactions are tokenized. Visa will modify interchange
  rates select transactions (see Table 3).
</span></p><style data-emotion="css 19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100">.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{color:#202020;font-family:PayPalOpen-Regular,"Helvetica href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/s-2024-all#_msoanchor_1"><span>[KV1]</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></div></div></div><h1><span>What is the Intra-Europe EEA Commercial Interchange Fees Mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>EU</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Dates</span></strong><span>: 13 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Visa will update intra-Europe EEA interchange fees for commercial cards. As a result of this
  change, ecommerce transactions will be aligned with Standard fee type. Merchants affected will be
  those processing the related card type and category:

          Debt Repayment; MCC 6211â€”Security Brokers/Dealers
        </span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><sup><span>3</span></sup><span> Charity: MCC 6012â€”Charitable Social Service Organizations</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><sup><span>4</span></sup><span> There will be no changes to the interchange rates for the Small Market
          Expense (EX) commercial product subtypes.
        </span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><sup><span>5</span></sup><span> There will be no changes to the interchange rates for the Large Market
          Enterprise (EN) commercial product subtypes.
        </span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><sup><span>6</span></sup><span> Visa Purchasing acquirers may receive an additional interchange incentive of
          EUR 0.50 if they submit the transaction with additional data.
          </span><b><span> Effective CPD 13 April 2024 </span></b><span>
          , the interchange incentive fee for additional data for Visa Purchasing with Fleet will be
          0.30% (per below.)
        </span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><sup><span>7</span></sup><span> There will be no changes to the Large Ticket Program</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h1><span>What is the Visa Introduction to CVV2 Pricing in Canada?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>Canada</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 1 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Visa will introduce acquirer pricing for Card Verification Value 2 (CVV2) in Canada. Fee is
  $0.0025 USD per CVV2 match/no match result. The fee will not be charged when 3D Secure (3DS) is
  successful or when the transaction is a zero-amount account verification message.
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Merchants who use CVV2 in Canada can expect to pay a fee. Merchants should adjust their strategy
  to avoid the fee (see Table 5 for fee details).
</span></p><style data-emotion="css 19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100">.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{color:#202020;font-family:PayPalOpen-Regular,"Helvetica 752px){.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{font-size:min(0.875rem, 28px);line-height:min(1.125rem, >td,.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >th{border-bottom:0.0625rem solid #545d68;border-top:0.0625rem solid transparent;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td{padding:0.75rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td:first-of-type{padding-left:1rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td:last-of-type{padding-right:1rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="197"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><b><span>Fee</span></b><b></b></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="185"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>2VAS70000</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="164"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>CVV2 â€“ ACQUIRER FEE</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="175"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Acquirer</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="197"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>$0.0025 USD per CVV2 match / no match result</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h1><span>What are the Updates to Visa Secure Data Fields mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEATURE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>Global</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 12 August 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Effective 12 August 2024, Visa will recategorize three existing 3D Secure (3DS) data fields from
  "conditional" to "required." These fields are passed in the 3DS Authentication Request (AReq) and
  provide additional information to improve the quality of authentication requests and potentially
  drive authorization rate performance. While previously communicated that Visa was planning to
  recategorize twelve fields (see Table 7), Visa updated their guidance in early 2024, pushing the
  new effective date to August and reducing the number of required fields from twelve to five and
  then to just three (see Table 6).
</span></p><style data-emotion="css 19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100">.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{color:#202020;font-family:PayPalOpen-Regular,"Helvetica 752px){.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100{font-size:min(0.875rem, 28px);line-height:min(1.125rem, 36px);}}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr{background-color:#f4f4f7;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td,.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >th{border-bottom:0.0625rem solid #545d68;border-top:0.0625rem solid transparent;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td{padding:0.75rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr >td:first-of-type{padding-left:1rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >tbody >tr #545d68;padding:0.75rem;}@media screen and (max-width: 752px){.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >thead>tr >th{font-size:min(0.875rem, 28px);line-height:min(1.125rem, 36px);}}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >thead>tr >th:last-of-type{padding-right:1rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 >thead>tr >th:first-of-type{padding-left:1rem;}.css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100 th{text-align:start;}</style><table data-ppui-info="table_3.22.1__7.46.3" class="ppvx_table ppvx_table-responsive-sm ecmTable articlesTable css-19859z6-text_body-legacy_table-text_body_strong-align_start-w100"><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" width="720"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Table 6 â€“ Data Field Requirements by Device Channel</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="360"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><b><span>Browser</span></b><b></b></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td width="360"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><b><span>In-App / Software Development Kit (SDK)</span></b><b></b></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td width="360"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Browser IP Address</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td><td rowspan="3" width="360"><p class="markdown-p"></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>Common Device Identification Parameters (Device IP Address)</span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr><tr><td   These updated fields provide Visa's Access Control Server (ACS) additional information,
  potentially helping to drive authorization rate performance and improve frictionless checkout.
  Transaction processing will not be impacted, but merchants are strongly advised to provide these
  fields to ensure compliance with Visa's operating rules. Visa may introduce a compliance deadline
  at a later date and assess potential non-compliance fees. We will send further communications when
  and if that will happen.
</span></p><style data-emotion="css           one of the two fields
        </span></p><p class="markdown-p"></p></td></tr></tbody></table><h1><span>What are the Visa Resolve Online Pricing Changes for Europe?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>EU</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date(s)</span></strong><span>: 1 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact:</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  Visa is updating pricing for their dispute tool, Visa Resolve Online (VROL) in Europe. Effective 1
  April 2024, Visa will introduce new fees for Pre-arbitration with Qualified Remedy and
  Collaboration Requests between acquirers and issuers. Visa are also increasing the existing fees
  applicable for case filing and response submission (applicable to over 21-day timeframe).
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  The updated fees will be reflected in invoicing from May 2024. Some of these fees are passed to
  merchants in the event of a lost dispute, so merchants need to be aware of potentially higher
  dispute fees. In addition, Visa is increasing the fees for access to VROL, which would impact
  internal operational cost only.
</span></p><h1><span>What is the Non-Domestic Currency Settlement Fee mandate?</span></h1><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span><span>FEE CHANGE</span></span></strong><span> | </span><strong><span><span>VISA</span></span></strong><span> |
  </span><strong><span>EU</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><a href="/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases"><span>Back to Overview Table</span></a></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Effective Date</span></strong><span>: 1 April 2024</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>Merchant Impact</span></strong></p><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  From 1 April 2024, Visa will increase the non-domestic settlement volume fee from 0.05% to 0.10%.
  This fee was introduced in 2022 and applies to merchants who process cross-border Visa payments in
  the EU and receive settlement in a currency different than the domestic currency of the acquirer
  (BIN or BIN range country).
</span></p><p class="markdown-p"><strong><span>The fee applies under the following conditions:</span></strong></p><ul class="list list--disc"><li><span>Transactions need to be identified as cross-border (intra-Europe or international)</span></li><li><span>
    The issuer chooses to settle the transactions with Visa (i.e., issuer settlement currency) in a
    different currency than the domestic currency of the Bank Identification Number (BIN) or BIN
    range country.
  </span></li><li><span>
    The acquirer chooses to settle the transactions with Visa (i.e., acquirer settlement currency)
    in a different currency than the domestic currency of the merchant country where the transaction
    is completed.
  </span></li></ul><p class="markdown-p"><span>
  The fee applies to merchants operating in the European Economic Area (EEA), Andorra, Israel,
  Monaco, San Marino, Switzerland, United Kingdom (including Gibraltar) and Vatican City State.
</span></p><div role="alert" class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__1QhIq ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert--note__gRM6J"><div class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__header__T2Wkg"><style data-emotion="css 4757ty-svg-size_xs">.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs{speak:none;display:inline-block;aspect-ratio:1;width:1.125rem;height:1.125rem;}.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs img,.css-4757ty-svg-size_xs svg{width:100%;height:100%;display:block;}</style><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__icon__puACD css-4757ty-svg-size_xs" data-ppui-info="icons_8.21.2" role="img" aria-label="note" data-ppui="true"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" fill="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 24 24" width="1em" height="1em" data-ppui="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M21 12a9 9 0 1 1-18 0 9 9 0 0 1 18 0zm-9.662 5h1.32c.18 0 .276-.096.276-.276v-5.925c0-.18-.096-.276-.276-.276h-1.32c-.18 0-.276.096-.276.276v5.925c0 .18.096.276.276.276zM12 9a1 1 0 1 0 0-2 1 1 0 0 0 0 2z" clip-rule="evenodd" data-ppui="true"></path></svg></span><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__title__FOcbD">Note</span><span class="ContextualAlert-module_pp-alert__content__2-Ddi"><ul class="list list--disc"><li><span>
      A cross-border transaction is where the merchant country location is different than the issuer
      country location.
    </span></li><li><span>
      An intra-Europe cross border transaction happens when both the issuer and merchant country
      location are within the Visa Europe territory.
    </span></li><li><span>
      An international cross border transaction in this context is where the issuer country location
      is within the Visa Europe territory and the merchant country location is outside the Visa
      Europe territory and vice versa
    </span></li></ul></span></div></div></section></div><nav class="right-nav-container"><h4 class="right-nav-title">On this page</h4><ul All Spring 2024 Network Updates\nslug: /articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/s-2024-all/\ncreateTime: '2025-04-02T01:09:22.991Z'\nupdateTime: '2025-04-02T01:09:23.061Z'\n---\n\n\n\n# All Spring 2024 Network Updates\n\n\n## SPRING 2024 RELEASE GUIDE\n\nThe card networks (Visa, Mastercard, Amex, Discover, etc.) introduce and make changes to their operating rules and mandates throughout the year. Many of these changes come twice per yearâ€”in spring and fall.\n\nThese network updates typically include fee introductions or fee changes, new mandates, new features, or updates to existing features. The changes can be broad in nature and may include updates such as mandates to comply with new regulations; implementing new fees; or requiring merchants to use schemes like 3DS 2.0 to help reduce fraud.\n\nWhile many of the updates require no action for merchants, some do require integration changes or force adoption of services. Additionally, some of the updates carry new or changed fees.\n\n**PayPal Braintree teams have worked together to identify the key updates for Spring 2024, and we have provided information about these updates below.** We have called out the type of update (fee change, mandate, new feature/update), which network the update comes from, and the relevant market(s).\n\nnew\n\n\n## **KEY SPRING 2024 NETWORK RELEASES**\n\n(click below to jump to specific update)\n\n| **Scheme** | **Name (click to jump)** | **Type** | **Geographic Impact** |\n| **Visa** | [Processing Integrity Fees](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/v-s24#what-are-the-visa-processing-integrity-fees) | Fee Change | CEMEA, CA, APAC, EU, LAC |\n| [Modifications to Certain US Interchange Rates and Programs](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/v-s24#what-are-the-modifications-to-certain-us-interchange-rates-and-programs) | Fee Change | US Change | US |\n| [Revising Acquirer Brand Volume Fee](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/2024/mc-s24#what-is-the-revising-acquirer-brand-volume-fee-change) | Fee Change | US |\n\n\n## All Mastercard Network Updates\n\n\n# What is the Expansion of the Digital Enablement Fee in the US mandate?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **Mastercard** | US\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 15 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nFrom 15 April 2024, Mastercard will revise the pricing for the Digital Enablement Fee (DEF) and charge a fixed rate of $0.40 USD for card-not-present (CNP) transactions greater than or equal to $1000 USD. The Digital Enablement Fee of 0.02% (2 basis points) with a minimum of $0.20 USD remains for transactions less than $1000 USD.\n\n\n# What is the Revised Excessive Authorization Attempts (CA) mandate?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **Mastercard** | CA\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 1 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nFrom 1 April 2024, Mastercard will revise the threshold for the Excessive Authorization Attempts Transaction Processing Excellence (TPE) program in Canada, introducing a threshold of 35 declined attempts on the same account number, at the same card acceptor, and for the same amount within a 30-day period.\n\n\n**NOTE**\n The first billing for the new Canada TPE threshold will occur on 5 May 2024.\n\n \n\nTo avoid the excessive authorization attempts TPE fees, Mastercard is recommending that acquirers immediately stop sending authorizations on the same card and same card acceptor ID, within a 24-hour period after receiving 10 consecutive decline responses, as well as to stop sending authorizations on the same card, same card acceptor, for the same amount, within a 30-day period after receiving 35 decline responses.\n\nThe applicable fee will be 0.50 USD per identified declined transaction. To avoid TPE fees, merchants should review their statements to identify TPE charges then adjust behavior to avoid these fees.\n\n\n# What is the CVV2 Compliance Requirements mandate?\n\n**FEATURE CHANGE** | **Mastercard** | APAC\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 8 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nMastercard will be eliminating the Card Verification Value 2 (CVV2) verification for both card-on-file (COF) and guest checkout experiences in the Asia Pacific region. This change will apply to all Mastercard Digital Enablement Service (MDES) tokenized transactions. By leveraging tokenization and approved authentication methods available through the EMV 3-D Secure and Token Authentication Framework (TAF), consumers can complete transactions securely without the need for CVV2 verification.\n\nNo merchant action is immediately required, but they should plan for when issuers are ready to incorporate the change.\n\n\n# What is the Extending Network Access and Brand Usage Fee change?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **Mastercard** | US\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 15 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nFrom 15 April 2024, Mastercard is extending the Network Access and Brand Usage fee (NABU) for Non-domestic Authorizations, Collection-only, and Refund/Credit transactions in the United States, increasing the fees for US merchants who process transactions from non-US issued cards to $0.0295 per transaction. NABU feesâ€”sometimes also referred to as card association fees or card brand feesâ€”are the fees associated with processing a transaction with a card network like Mastercard.\n\n| Table 8 â€“ Extending Network Access and Brand Usage Fee |\n|  | **Merchant Country is U.S.** |\n| **Issuer Country is U.S.** | $0.0195 |\n| **Issuer Country is non-U.S.** | $0.0295 |\n\n\n# What is the Revising Acquirer Brand Volume Fee change?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **Mastercard** | US\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 15 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nFrom 15 April 2024, Mastercard will introduce two enhanced tools (Merchant Risk Dashboard; Small Business Credit Analytics) designed to streamline acquirersâ€™ efforts to identify and mitigate potential risks during both the initial onboarding process and daily operations. In addition, Mastercard will raise the Acquirer Brand Volume fee by 0.01% from 0.13% to 0.14%. This updated fee will apply to all Mastercard transactions.\n\n\n## All Visa Network Updates\n\n\n# What are the Visa Processing Integrity Fees?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **VISA** | **CEMEA, CA, AP, EU, Latin America and the Caribbean**\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date:** 1 April 2024 (APAC excluding Japan); 25 April 2024 (CEMEA, EU, LAC excluding Brazil and Chile); 25 May 2024 (Canada)\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nVisa will begin compliance monitoring for the Processing Integrity Program with the introduction of 2 new fees:\n\n\n- **Misuse of Authorization System**: assessed to approved or partially approved auth transactions that cannot be matched to a clearing transactions or authorization reversal.\n- **Unmatched Clearing**: assessed on clearing transactions that cannot be matched to previously approved or partially approved auth transactions.\n\n| Region | Previous  Effective Date | Updated Effective Date | Fee Rate (per transaction) |\n| CEMEA | 10/1/23 | 4/25/24 | $0.05 |\n| Canada | 1/25/24 | 5/25/24 | $0.05 |\n| APACâ€¯(excluding Japan) | 4/1/24 | 4/1/24 | $0.05 |\n| EU* | 7/1/23 | 4/25/24 | $0.01 |\n| LAC (excluding Brazil / Chile) | 7/1/23 | 4/25/24 | $0.05 |\n| *EU rate rises to $0.05 per transaction in July 2024. |\n\n\n# What are the Modifications to Certain US Interchange Rates and Programs?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **VISA** | **US**\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date:** 13 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nInterchange adjustments based on Visa products used by the merchants' consumers. Merchants will see continued interchange savings when transactions are tokenized. Fee is $0.0025 USD per CVV2 match/no match result. The fee will not be charged when 3D Secure (3DS) is successful or when the transaction is a zero-amount account verification message.\n\nMerchants who use CVV2 in Canada can expect to pay a fee. Merchants should adjust their strategy to avoid the fee (see Table 5 for fee details).\n\n| Table 5 â€“ Card Verification Value Acquirer Fee (Canada) |\n| Billing Line | Billing Line Description | Assessed To | Fee |\n| 2VAS70000 | CVV2 â€“ ACQUIRER FEE | Acquirer | $0.0025 USD per CVV2 match / no match result |\n\n\n# What are the Updates to Visa Secure Data Fields mandate?\n\n**FEATURE CHANGE** | **VISA** | **Global**\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 12 August 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nEffective 12 August 2024, Visa will recategorize three existing 3D Secure (3DS) data fields from \"conditional\" to \"required.\" These fields are passed in the 3DS Authentication Request (AReq) and provide additional information to improve the quality of authentication requests and potentially drive authorization rate performance. While previously communicated that Visa was planning to recategorize twelve fields (see Table 7), Visa updated their guidance in early 2024, pushing the new effective date to August and reducing the number of required fields from twelve to five and then to just three (see Table 6).\n\n| Table 6 â€“ Data Field Requirements by Device Channel |\n| Browser | In-App / Software Development Kit (SDK) |\n| Browser IP Address | Common Device Identification Parameters (Device IP Address) |\n| Browser Screen Height |\n| Browser Screen Width |\n\nThese updated fields provide Visa's Access Control Server (ACS) additional information, potentially helping to drive authorization rate performance and improve frictionless checkout. Transaction processing will not be impacted, but merchants are strongly advised to provide these fields to ensure compliance with Visa's operating rules. Visa may introduce a compliance deadline at a later date and assess potential non-compliance fees. We will send further communications when and if that will happen.\n\n| Table 7 â€“ No longer required Data Fields |\n| Priority Data Fields | Requirement Status | Update from previous announcements |\n| Browser IP Address 1 | Mandatory (Browser) | No Update |\n| Browser Screen Height 1 | Mandatory (Browser) | No Update |\n| Browser Screen Width 1 | Mandatory (Browser) | No Update |\n| Common Device Identification   Parameters (Device IP Address) 2 | Mandatory (In-App) | No Update |\n| Cardholder Billing Address City 3 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Billing Address Country 3 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Billing Address Line 1 3 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Billing Address Postal Code 3 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Billing Address State 3 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Email Address | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Name | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| Cardholder Phone Number 4, 5 | Recommended | No Longer Mandatory |\n| 1 Only for browser-based transactions\n\n\n\n\n\n2 Only for SDK transactions\n\n\n\n\n\n3 Except in markets where the billing address fields do not exist.\n\n\n\n\n\n4 At least one phone number (work / home / mobile) is recommended.\n\n\n\n\n\n5 Merchants are recommended to pass the Cardholder Phone Number and Cardholder Email Address fields for authentication, but merchants will be compliant if they only pass one of the two fields |\n\n\n# What are the Visa Resolve Online Pricing Changes for Europe?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **VISA** | **EU**\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date(s)** : 1 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact:**\n\nVisa is updating pricing for their dispute tool, Visa Resolve Online (VROL) in Europe. Effective 1 April 2024, Visa will introduce new fees for Pre-arbitration with Qualified Remedy and Collaboration Requests between acquirers and issuers. Visa are also increasing the existing fees applicable for case filing and response submission (applicable to over 21-day timeframe).\n\nThe updated fees will be reflected in invoicing from May 2024. Some of these fees are passed to merchants in the event of a lost dispute, so merchants need to be aware of potentially higher dispute fees. In addition, Visa is increasing the fees for access to VROL, which would impact internal operational cost only.\n\n\n# What is the Non-Domestic Currency Settlement Fee mandate?\n\n**FEE CHANGE** | **VISA** | **EU**\n\n[Back to Overview Table](/braintree/articles/risk-and-security/compliance/network-updates/overview#key-spring-2024-network-releases)\n\n**Effective Date** : 1 April 2024\n\n**Merchant Impact**\n\nFrom 1 April 2024, Visa will increase the non-domestic settlement volume fee from 0.05% to 0.10%. This fee was introduced in 2022 and applies to merchants who process cross-border Visa payments in the EU and receive settlement in a currency different than the domestic currency of the acquirer (BIN or BIN range country).\n\n**The fee applies under the following conditions:**\n\n\n- Transactions need to be identified as cross-border (intra-Europe or international)\n- The issuer chooses to settle the transactions with Visa (i.e., issuer settlement currency) in a different currency than the domestic currency of the Bank Identification Number (BIN) or BIN range country.\n- The acquirer chooses to settle the transactions with Visa (i.e., acquirer settlement currency) in a different currency than the domestic currency of the merchant country where the transaction is completed.\n\nThe fee applies to merchants operating in the European Economic Area (EEA), Andorra, Israel, Monaco, San Marino, Switzerland, United Kingdom (including Gibraltar) and Vatican City State.\n\n\n**NOTE**\n \n- A cross-border transaction is where the merchant country location is different than the issuer country location.\n- An intra-Europe cross border transaction happens when both the issuer and merchant country location are within the Visa Europe territory.\n- An international cross border transaction in this context is where the issuer country location is within the Visa Europe territory and the merchant country location is outside the Visa Europe territory and vice versa\n\n \n\n"},"routes/braintree/articles":null},"actionData":null,"errors":null},"future":{"v2_dev":true,"unstable_postcss":false,"unstable_tailwind":false,"v2_errorBoundary":false,"v2_headers":false,"v2_meta":true,"v2_normalizeFormMethod":false,"v2_routeConvention":false}};</script><script nonce="hKE7+ta55xm3XJSp4Ki3Au3qGCSdhLHwV+i8QvlREYaEfWGg" type="module" async="">import "https://www.paypalobjects.com/btdevdoc/bundles/4.3.24/manifest-D829D641.js";
